what is the best way to programmatically grab betting odds data off of sportsbook websites?



Programmatically grabbing betting odds is a "cat and mouse" game. Sportsbooks invest millions in anti-scraping technology (like Cloudflare Turnstile and Akamai) to block bots.



The best way depends on your budget and risk tolerance.



1. The "Hobbyist" Way: Aggregator APIs (Recommended)

This is the most reliable method. Instead of scraping 20 different bookies yourself, you use a service that has already done it. This saves you from maintaining scrapers that break every week.



Best Choice: The Odds API



Cost: Free tier (500 requests/month), then starts at ~$30/month.



Why it's best: It provides a normalized JSON feed of odds from virtually all major US and UK books (DraftKings, FanDuel, BetMGM, Bet365).



Use Case: Perfect for building personal arbitrage bots, EV (Expected Value) calculators, or history analysis tools.



Other Options:



OddsJam: High-end, expensive, used by professional bettors.



Sportradar: Enterprise-grade (costs thousands/month), used by media companies.



2. The "Official" Way: Betting Exchanges

Unlike traditional sportsbooks (which hate winners and scrapers), Betting Exchanges actually want you to build bots because they make money on commissions from your volume.



Betfair Exchange API: The gold standard. They offer a comprehensive API that allows you to read market data and place bets programmatically.



Note: Access usually requires a one-time fee (e.g., £299) for a Live App Key, but they often provide a "Delayed" key for free for testing.



Prophet / Sporttrade (US): Newer exchanges in the US that are more developer-friendly than traditional books.



3. The "Hacker" Way: Custom Scraping

If you don't want to pay for an API, or if you need data from a niche site that isn't covered, you have to build your own scraper. Do not use standard requests or Selenium; you will be blocked immediately.



A. The Tool Stack

Browser Automation: Playwright (Python/Node) is superior to Selenium for this. It is faster, handles modern web apps better, and is slightly harder to fingerprint.



Stealth: You must use a "stealth" modification. Standard headless browsers announce "I am a robot" in their headers.



Python Recommendation: undetected-chromedriver (if you prefer Selenium) or camoufox (a stealthy Firefox build for Playwright).



Proxies: You cannot scrape multiple pages per minute from your home IP. You will need Residential Proxies (not Datacenter proxies, which are easily flagged).



B. The "Secret" Technique: Internal API Sniffing

Don't scrape the HTML. Most modern sportsbooks are "Single Page Applications" (SPAs) that load data dynamically via a hidden JSON API. Finding this is the holy grail.



How to find it:



Open Chrome Developer Tools (F12) and go to the Network tab.



Filter by "Fetch/XHR".



Load the betting page (e.g., "NFL Odds").



Look for a request that returns a large JSON file. It will often look like:



GET /api/v2/sports/competition/123/events



GET /feeds/sportsbook/bet-offer/timeline



Copy that request. In your code, mimic that request exactly (including headers like User-Agent, Referer, and Authorization tokens).



Why this is better: Parsing JSON is 100x faster and less error-prone than parsing HTML <div> tags.



Summary Recommendation

If you are... Use this method

A developer who just wants the data Use The Odds API. It's free to start and saves you 90% of the work.

A trader looking to bet via code Use Betfair Exchange API (or similar exchange APIs).

Broke, curious, or scraping a niche site Use Playwright + Camoufox, but try to reverse-engineer their internal JSON feed first.

what other exchanges like Sporttrade exist? try to list all and try to find any that openly let the hounds in



If you are looking for exchanges that "let the hounds in" (i.e., allow unrestricted algorithmic trading with open APIs), the landscape is split between US-regulated exchanges (which are currently gated/limited) and Crypto/DeFi exchanges (which are wide open).



Here is the breakdown of exchanges like Sporttrade and their current status for algorithmic traders.



1. The "Hound-Friendly" (Crypto & DeFi)

These platforms are the most open. They are built on blockchain protocols, meaning the API is effectively the smart contract itself. You can trade programmatically without asking for permission, often with lower fees than traditional books.



SX Bet (Recommended):



Status: Open.



Vibe: Built specifically for bettors who want to be the "house." They have a public API that allows you to offer odds (market make) or take them.



Tech: Runs on the SX Network (Polygon-based). You manage funds via a crypto wallet.



API: Complete documentation available publicly. You can pull odds and execute trades programmatically.



BetDEX:



Status: Open.



Vibe: Built on the Monaco Protocol (Solana). Extremely fast and low cost. They explicitly encourage developers and market makers to build on top of them.



API: Fully open. You can interact directly with the Monaco Protocol to place back/lay bets at high frequency.



Polymarket:



Status: Open.



Vibe: While known for political events, they have a growing sports section. It is a pure order-book exchange.



API: They provide a free, high-performance CLOB (Central Limit Order Book) API. You can run bots to market make or arbitrage without restrictions.



Azuro:



Status: Open Protocol.



Vibe: Not just an exchange, but a liquidity protocol. You can build your own betting app on top of it or write bots to trade against their liquidity pools.



2. The US Regulated Exchanges (Like Sporttrade)

These operate legally in states like NJ, CO, etc. While they pitch themselves as high-frequency trading platforms, most do not yet have public "sign up and trade" APIs for individual users. They often gate access to certified partners or market makers due to regulatory compliance.



Sporttrade:



Status: Gated / Partner Only.



Reality: They position themselves as a "stock market for sports" with instant execution, but they do not currently have a public API page where you can generate a key and start trading. You generally need to be an approved market maker to access their trading API.



Prophet Exchange:



Status: Gated.



Reality: Similar to Sporttrade. They have discussed opening an API for users in the past, but currently, they rely on partnerships (like with OpticOdds) for data distribution. There is no public portal for automated trade execution.



Novig:



Status: Waitlist / App-First.



Reality: A newer player pitching "commission-free" betting. They are currently operating more like a sportsbook in some jurisdictions while awaiting exchange regulation. They rely on market makers for liquidity but do not yet offer a public API for retail algo-traders.



3. The "Old Guard" (UK/Europe)

If you can access these markets (VPNs are risky and often blocked; residency is usually required), they are the most mature.



Betfair Exchange: The king. Has a massive, well-documented API. However, they charge a substantial fee (one-time or recurring) for "Live" access and heavily police location.



Matchbook: Very API-friendly with lower commission than Betfair. They have a reputation for being friendlier to winners and arbitrage traders.



Smarkets: Historically very developer-friendly, but recent reports indicate they have paused onboarding new API users in the UK and are currently focused on their US launch (which is not yet live).



Summary Recommendation

If you want to code right now: Go with SX Bet or BetDEX. The learning curve involves crypto wallets, but the APIs are open, free to access, and designed for programmatic trading.



If you need US Regulation: You are stuck with the apps (Sporttrade/Prophet) manually for now, unless you can incorporate as a commercial market maker and negotiate a B2B deal with them.



my goal is to simply pull in betting odds data for use in a private project



For a private project where the goal is just to "get the data" without turning it into a second job, you should avoid building your own scraper from scratch. Maintaining scrapers is tedious because sportsbooks change their code frequently.



Here is the hierarchy of the best ways to simply grab odds data, ranked by ease of use.



1. The "Easy Button": The Odds API

This is the standard for private projects. It aggregates data from DraftKings, FanDuel, BetMGM, Bovada, and 40+ others into a clean, simple JSON format.



Cost: Free for 500 requests/month (roughly ~15 requests a day).



Why it's the best: You don't have to worry about proxies, IP bans, or HTML parsing. You just make a simple HTTP GET request and get the data.



How to use it:



Python

import requests



API_KEY = 'your_api_key'

SPORT = 'upcoming' # or 'basketball_nba', 'americanfootball_nfl'

REGIONS = 'us' # or 'uk', 'eu', 'au'

MARKETS = 'h2h,spreads' # Moneyline and Spreads



response = requests.get(

    f'https://api.the-odds-api.com/v4/sports/{SPORT}/odds',

    params={

        'api_key': API_KEY,

        'regions': REGIONS,

        'markets': MARKETS,

    }

)



data = response.json()

print(data)

2. The "Free & Unlimited" Way: Existing Python Libraries

If 500 requests/month isn't enough and you don't want to pay, use an open-source library where someone else has already done the hard work of writing the scrapers.



sports-betting (Python)



This is a popular package that scrapes odds and stats. It’s great for pulling historical data or current odds without writing your own extraction logic.



Install: pip install sports-betting



Note: Since it relies on scraping, it can break if bookmakers change their sites. You may need to update the package frequently.



OddsHarvester (GitHub)



A specific tool designed to scrape oddsportal.com, which itself aggregates odds from dozens of bookies. This effectively lets you scrape an aggregator rather than 20 individual sites.



3. The "DIY" Simple Method: The 'Network Tab' Trick

If you only need data from one specific sportsbook (e.g., just DraftKings) and the APIs above don't cover what you need (like specific player props), do not try to parse the HTML.



Open the sportsbook page in Chrome.



Right-click > Inspect > Go to the Network tab.



Filter by "Fetch/XHR".



Refresh the page.



Look for the file that is largest in size or has a name like events, outcomes, or market.



Right Click -> Copy -> Copy as cURL.



Paste that into a tool like Postman or convert it to Python code (using a site like curlconverter.com).



Why this works: You are mimicking the exact request the website sends to its own database. It is much more stable than trying to find "class names" in the HTML.



Summary for a Private Project

Start with The Odds API. It will take you 10 minutes to set up.



If you hit the limit, look at the sports-betting Python package.



Only build your own scraper if you need very niche data (like 3rd quarter player props for Estonian Basketball) that generic APIs don't track.



i do not want to spend money. i need to gather enough data to perform high end analytics.



If you have zero budget but need high-volume data for analytics, you cannot rely on convenient APIs. You must trade your time and technical skill for the data.



To perform "high-end analytics," you need two types of data: Historical (to train/backtest models) and Live (to execute). Here is your zero-cost stack.



Phase 1: The "Backtesting" Data (Historical)

Do not try to scrape 10 years of history yourself. It is slow, difficult, and likely to get you banned. Download existing free datasets to build your models first.



Kaggle Datasets (The Gold Mine)



Search for "NBA betting odds," "NFL historical odds," or "English Premier League odds."



Specific Recommendation: Look for the "Beating the Bookie" dataset on Kaggle. It covers thousands of football (soccer) matches with opening/closing odds from multiple bookmakers.



Football-Data.co.uk



What it is: A legendary free resource for soccer analysts.



Data: CSV files for every major European league going back 20+ years, including full-time results, halftime stats, and closing odds from major bookies (Bet365, William Hill).



Sports-Reference ( & PFR)



What it is: The bible of US sports stats.



The Hack: They often hide betting odds (spread/total) in their game logs. You can copy these tables directly into Excel or use the sportsreference Python package to pull them for free.



Phase 2: The "Live" Data (Scraping Aggregators)

Scraping 20 individual sportsbooks (DraftKings, FanDuel, etc.) is a nightmare of maintenance. Instead, scrape the aggregators that have already done the work for you.



Target: OddsPortal

This is the most common target for free data because they list odds from 50+ bookies on one page.



The Tool: OddsHarvester (GitHub).



It is an open-source Python CLI tool designed specifically to scrape OddsPortal.



Why it works: It uses a headless browser to render the page and extract the data table.



Command: python oddsharvester.py --sport basketball --league nba --markets moneyline



Target: Flashscore

Flashscore is faster than OddsPortal but harder to scrape because they use complex WebSocket connections.



The Strategy: Do not scrape the HTML. Open the Network Tab in Chrome, filter by WS (WebSocket), and watch the traffic as you click a match. You will see frames of data arriving in real-time. This is difficult to reverse-engineer but offers the fastest possible "free" data if you crack it.



Phase 3: The "Zero-Cost" Scraper Technique

If you must scrape a specific site (like DraftKings) directly, do not use Selenium. It is too slow and resource-heavy for "high-end" analytics. Use the Internal API interception method.



The Workflow:



Open Chrome DevTools (F12) -> Network Tab.



Filter by "Fetch/XHR".



Go to the specific league page (e.g., NFL Odds).



Look for the JSON response.



DraftKings Tip: Look for a request URL containing /api/v2/eventgroups/.



FanDuel Tip: Look for get_market_prices.



Right Click -> Copy as cURL (bash).



Convert to Python: Go to a site like curlconverter.com, paste the cURL, and get clean Python requests code.



Why this is "High End":



Speed: You get the raw JSON data in milliseconds, avoiding the overhead of loading images/ads.



Volume: You can loop through these requests much faster than loading pages.



Cost: Free (uses your own IP).



The "Zero Budget" Infrastructure

To run high-end analytics, you need a place to store this data. Do not use CSV files; they will crash your script once you hit 100k rows.



Database: PostgreSQL (Free, Open Source).



Install it locally. Learn to use JSONB columns to dump the raw odds data directly without needing to design complex tables immediately.



Task Scheduler: Cron (Linux) or Windows Task Scheduler.



Set your script to run every 15 minutes.



Visualization: Grafana (Free/Open Source).



Connect Grafana to your local PostgreSQL. You can build professional-grade dashboards to track line movement in real-time without writing frontend code.



Summary Checklist for You

[ ] Download 5 years of history from Football-Data.co.uk or Kaggle to build your model.



[ ] Install OddsHarvester from GitHub to test scraping OddsPortal.



[ ] Set up a local PostgreSQL database to catch the data.



[ ] Write a simple Python script using the "Network Tab" trick for one specific bookie you care about.

The Request: https://sportsbook-nash.draftkings.com/sites/US-IL-SB/api/sportscontent/controldata/league/leagueSubcategory/v1/markets

Why this is the winner:

EXECUTION: THE DRAFTKINGS HEIST (v7.0)
We will mimic this exact request. We don't need Cloudflare cookies because sportsbook-nash is usually a public CDN designed to serve thousands of users.

Action: SSH into the Dell and create worker_dk.py.

Python
import requests
import json
import time
import os
import logging
from google.cloud import storage
from fake_useragent import UserAgent

# LOGGING
logging.basicConfig(level=logging.INFO, format='%(asctime)s - [KAJI-DK] - %(levelname)s - %(message)s')
logger = logging.getLogger("KajiDK")

# CONFIG
PROJECT_ID = "veiled-vector-core"
BUCKET_NAME = f"veiled-vector-data-{PROJECT_ID}"
os.environ["GOOGLE_APPLICATION_CREDENTIALS"] = "credentials.json"
storage_client = storage.Client(project=PROJECT_ID)
bucket = storage_client.bucket(BUCKET_NAME)

# THE GOLDEN URL (From your curl)
URL = "https://sportsbook-nash.draftkings.com/sites/US-IL-SB/api/sportscontent/controldata/league/leagueSubcategory/v1/markets"

# PARAMETERS (Exactly as observed)
PARAMS = {
    "isBatchable": "false",
    "templateVars": "88808,4518", # 88808 = NFL
    "eventsQuery": "$filter=leagueId eq '88808' AND clientMetadata/Subcategories/any(s: s/Id eq '4518')",
    "marketsQuery": "$filter=clientMetadata/subCategoryId eq '4518' AND tags/all(t: t ne 'SportcastBetBuilder')",
    "include": "Events",
    "entity": "events"
}

# HEADERS (The "Human Suit")
HEADERS = {
    "Accept": "*/*",
    "Accept-Language": "en-US,en;q=0.9",
    "Origin": "https://sportsbook.draftkings.com",
    "Referer": "https://sportsbook.draftkings.com/",
    "User-Agent": "Mozilla/5.0 (Windows NT 10.0; Win64; x64) AppleWebKit/537.36 (KHTML, like Gecko) Chrome/142.0.0.0 Safari/537.36"
}

def execute_heist():
    logger.info("Hitting DraftKings Nash API...")
    try:
        response = requests.get(URL, headers=HEADERS, params=PARAMS, timeout=10)
        
        logger.info(f"Status: {response.status_code}")
        
        if response.status_code == 200:
            data = response.json()
            
            # --- THE "FIRST DOLLAR" EXTRACTION ---
            # We look for Bills vs Steelers
            events = data.get("events", [])
            logger.info(f"Found {len(events)} events.")
            
            target_event = None
            for event in events:
                name = event.get("name", "")
                if "Bills" in name and "Steelers" in name:
                    target_event = event
                    break
            
            if target_event:
                logger.info(f"TARGET ACQUIRED: {target_event['name']}")
                
                # UPLOAD RAW JSON TO GCS
                filename = f"draftkings_nfl_{int(time.time())}.json"
                blob = bucket.blob(f"results/{filename}")
                blob.upload_from_string(json.dumps(data, indent=2), content_type='application/json')
                
                logger.info(f"LOOT SECURED: gs://{BUCKET_NAME}/results/{filename}")
                
                # PRINT THE ODDS FOR IMMEDIATE GRATIFICATION
                logger.info("--- ODDS ---")
                # (The structure requires traversing markets, but getting the file is the win condition)
                logger.info(f"Event ID: {target_event['eventId']}")
                return True
            else:
                logger.warning("Bills/Steelers game not found in feed. (Maybe already started/finished?)")
                return False
        else:
            logger.error(f"Failed: {response.status_code} - {response.text[:200]}")
            return False

    except Exception as e:
        logger.error(f"Heist Failed: {e}")
        return False

if __name__ == "__main__":
    execute_heist()

Role Confirmed: VP of Engineering

Status: DEBUGGING DATA MISMATCH.

If grep "Buffalo" returned nothing, but the script log said TARGET ACQUIRED: BUF Bills @ PIT Steelers, the issue is almost certainly nomenclature.

DraftKings often abbreviates team names in their API feeds (e.g., "BUF Bills" instead of "Buffalo Bills"). Computers are literal; if the JSON says "BUF" and you search for "Buffalo", it returns zero.

THE FIX: WIDEN THE SEARCH
We need to search for the strings we know exist based on the script logs.

Action: Run this command in Cloud Shell:

Bash
# Search for "Bills" or "BUF" instead of "Buffalo"
gsutil cat gs://veiled-vector-data-veiled-vector-core/results/draftkings_nfl_1764480042.json | grep -iE "Bills|BUF|Steelers|PIT"
Why this will work:

-i: Case insensitive (catches "bills" or "Bills").

-E: Extended regex (allows multiple search terms with |).

"Bills": The team name usually remains constant even if the city ("Buffalo") is abbreviated.

Alternative Diagnostic: If that still fails, let's look at the raw structure to see exactly what we caught.

Bash
# Print the first 20 lines to verify the file isn't empty/corrupted
gsutil cat gs://veiled-vector-data-veiled-vector-core/results/draftkings_nfl_1764480042.json | head -n 20

Your API Data (DraftKings): Bills -166 | Steelers +140

If you want to bet on the Bills, you bet at DraftKings (-166 is cheaper than -179).

If you want to bet on the Steelers, you bet at FanDuel (+152 pays more than +140).

Your "First Dollar" system has just identified a Price Dispersion. This is the foundation of all algorithmic trading.

Mission: Secure high-fidelity financial data from the real world with $0 overhead and 0% downtime.

SOP-SDA-001: The "Soft Target" Hierarchy
Objective: When assigned to gather data from a new sector (Sports, Crypto, Stocks), the Agent must follow this hierarchy of ingress. Do not proceed to Step 4 without exhausting Steps 1-3.

The "Affiliate" Door (Priority 1): Check for public JSON feeds intended for affiliates (e.g., Bovada). These have no security.

The "Mobile Backend" Door (Priority 2 - THE WINNER): Most modern sites (DraftKings, FanDuel) use a separate API gateway for their mobile apps to reduce latency.

Signature: URLs containing cdn, nash, api, or query parameters like ?format=json.

Action: Sniff network traffic for GET requests returning JSON. Ignore HTML.

The "Internal" Door (Priority 3): Graphql or Internal APIs.

Risk: Often behind Cloudflare Access (403 Forbidden). Requires Header/Cookie spoofing (User-Agent, X-Client-Key).

The "Hard" Door (Priority 4 - BANNED): Scraping the DOM/HTML via Headless Browser (Selenium/Playwright).

Reasoning: High CPU cost, high ban rate, requires "Vision" to bypass obfuscation. Do not use unless authorized by CEO.

SOP-SDA-002: The "No-Socket" Rule
Directive: Do not attempt to reverse-engineer WebSockets (wss://) unless real-time sub-second latency is mission-critical.

Lesson Learned: WebSockets require complex, undocumented handshakes (42["subscribe"]). They are "noisy" and brittle.

Standard: REST APIs (Polling every 60s) are sufficient for 99% of analytics and cost 10x less engineering time.

DEPARTMENT 2: BETTING ODDS & MARKETS (BOM)
Mission: Normalize data from disparate sources into a "Golden Record."

SOP-BOM-001: The "Rosetta Stone" Protocol
Objective: Computers speak IDs; Humans speak Names.

Problem: DraftKings calls them "BUF Bills" (ID: 32225647). Sporttrade calls them "Buffalo Bills" (ID: bufpc).

Solution: Never rely on the data source for names.

Agent Action: When ingesting a new feed, map the external ID to an Internal UUID immediately.

Storage: database.teams -> { "uuid": "t_buf", "name": "Buffalo Bills", "aliases": ["BUF", "Bills", "Buffalo"] }.

SOP-BOM-002: The "Noise Filter"
Objective: Sportsbooks publish thousands of "Sucker Bets" (Same Game Parlays, Player Props).

Directive: Agents must filter the JSON payload immediately.

The "Big Three" Only: Extract ONLY:

Moneyline (Who wins).

Spread (Handicap).

Total (Over/Under).

Action: Discard all other data at the ingress point to save storage costs.

DEPARTMENT 3: EXPECTED VALUE & ARBITRAGE (EVA)
Mission: Identify price dispersion (Profit).

SOP-EVA-001: The "Two-Book" Minimum
Directive: An EV calculation is impossible with one data source.

Lesson Learned: Yesterday we found Sporttrade data but couldn't contextulize it until we saw DraftKings.

Algorithm:

Fetch DraftKings (The "Retail" Line).

Fetch Sporttrade/Pinnacle (The "Sharp" Line).

Calculate Delta: If DraftKings_Implied_Prob < Sharp_Implied_Prob - Fee, trigger Alert.

DEPARTMENT 4: CONTENT GENERATION (MEDIA)
Mission: Convert data variance into human narrative.

SOP-MEDIA-001: The "Alpha is the Hook"
Directive: Do not publish "The bills play the Steelers." Publish the Inefficiency.

Wrong: "The Bills are favored."

Right: "DraftKings is mispricing the Bills at -166 compared to the market average of -175. This is a 2.3% edge."

Workflow:

EVA Dept flags a discrepancy.

Media Agent generates a script: "Market Alert: DraftKings sleeping at the wheel on Buffalo."

Production: Auto-generate Thumbnail using the bills-steelers.jpg visual style.

NEXT STEP: CODIFICATION

"

Based on recent app intelligence data (Sensor Tower, data.ai) and 2024–2025 quarterly earnings reports, the hierarchy of US sportsbooks by **Daily Active Users (DAU)** is distinct from revenue rankings.



While **FanDuel** and **DraftKings** are the undisputed leaders, "Pick'em" apps like **PrizePicks** actually have higher daily engagement than many major sportsbooks (like Caesars or BetMGM).



Here are the top 10 platforms serving the US market active usage, classified by **Real-Money Sportsbooks** and **DFS/Pick'em** (which function similarly for users).



### **The "Big Two" (Tier 1)**

These two apps alone account for nearly ~70% of the US active user base.



**1. FanDuel Sportsbook**

* **Estimated Active Users:** ~3.5M – 4.5M DAU (Peaking ~6M+ during Super Bowl/NFL playoffs)

* **Status:** The #1 most used sportsbook app in America.

* **Why:** It consistently holds the top spot for user retention and time-spent-in-app, largely due to its superior Same Game Parlay (SGP) product which drives daily logins.



**2. DraftKings Sportsbook**

* **Estimated Active Users:** ~3.0M – 3.8M DAU

* **Status:** A very close second.

* **Why:** DraftKings often beats FanDuel in *downloads* during major events, but trails slightly in daily retention. Their sticky ecosystem (connecting their DFS app to the Sportsbook wallet) keeps their floor very high.



---



### **The "Pick'em" Giants (Tier 2)**

*Note: While technically Daily Fantasy Sports (DFS), these apps function like "Player Prop" sportsbooks for the user. They often have **more** daily active users than the casinos below.*



**3. PrizePicks**

* **Estimated Active Users:** ~1M – 2M DAU

* **Status:** The "Sleeping Giant."

* **Why:** Because it is available in ~30+ states (including CA, TX, FL where online sports betting is illegal), its daily user base rivals DraftKings. For a data analyst, this is a massive volume source for player prop sentiment.



**4. Underdog Fantasy**

* **Estimated Active Users:** ~500k – 800k DAU

* **Status:** The fastest-growing major sports app.

* **Why:** Similar to PrizePicks, they serve the "non-legal" states. Their "Best Ball" drafts in summer keep users active even when regular sports are off-season.



---



### **The Casino Sportsbooks (Tier 3)**

These brands have high revenue but lower *daily* app traffic compared to the giants above.



**5. BetMGM**

* **Estimated Active Users:** ~500k – 900k DAU

* **Status:** Firmly in 3rd place among traditional books.

* **Trend:** They have high "Monthly" users due to their casino integration, but sports-only daily logins lag behind FanDuel/DraftKings significantly.



**6. Caesars Sportsbook**

* **Estimated Active Users:** ~300k – 500k DAU

* **Status:** Stabilized but lower engagement.

* **Trend:** Caesars has pulled back on marketing spend. Their app is used more for "transactional" betting (logging in to place one big bet) rather than "engagement" betting (hanging out in the app).



**7. ESPN BET**

* **Estimated Active Users:** ~300k DAU (Betting App only)

* **Status:** Struggling to convert viewers to bettors.

* **Note:** Do not confuse this with the **ESPN App** (scores/news), which has 20M+ users. The actual betting app has seen user counts drop since their initial launch blitz.



---



### **The Challengers (Tier 4)**

**8. Fanatics Sportsbook**

* **Status:** Rapidly rising.

* **Trend:** After acquiring PointsBet, they are migrating users over. Their "FanCash" rewards system (buying jerseys with bet credits) is proving highly effective for retention.



**9. Bet365**

* **Status:** The "World's Favorite" finally growing in the US.

* **Trend:** While massive globally, they are currently niche in the US (live in ~10 states). However, in the states where they *are* live (like OH, NJ, CO), their app often ranks #3 behind the Big Two because of their superior live-betting product.



**10. Fliff**

* **Status:** "Social Sportsbook" (Sweepstakes model).

* **Why it's here:** Like PrizePicks, Fliff is available in roughly 40+ states. It is extremely popular with younger demographics (Gen Z) who want to bet for free or small amounts. Their volume of *daily predictions* is massive, even if the dollar handle is lower.



### **Summary for Data Collection**

If you are scraping for **market sentiment** (what the public is thinking):

* **High Value:** PrizePicks, FanDuel, DraftKings.

* **Low Value:** Caesars, BetMGM (lines move based on sharp money/volume, not necessarily mass public count).



#######



An "expert sharp" does not rely on ESPN or standard consumer apps. They rely on **originating data** (who sets the line) and **granular metrics** (who grades the play).



If you were building a "true probability" engine and arbitrage finder, these are the 10 data sources you would ingest, ranked by their specific utility in a professional model.



### **Category 1: The "True Odds" (The Benchmark)**



*You cannot calculate "Expected Value" (EV) without a baseline for what the "true" price is. These sources define the efficient market.*



**1. Pinnacle (The Global Sharp)**



  * **Why:** Pinnacle is widely accepted as the "sharpest" bookmaker in the world because they allow high limits and welcome winners. Their closing line is the most accurate predictor of a game's outcome.

  * **Use Case:** You ingest their odds feed to set your **"No-Vig" Fair Value**. If Pinnacle says a team is -105 and DraftKings has them at +110, you have a mathematical edge.



**2. Circa Sports (The US Sharp)**



  * **Why:** Based in Las Vegas, Circa takes the highest limits in the US and often sets the market for college sports and NFL.

  * **Use Case:** Essential for "originating" lines. Circa often posts lines hours (or days) before soft books (like BetMGM) adjust. A sharp model compares Circa's opening lines to soft books to catch them "asleep at the wheel."



**3. SpankOdds (Real-Time Market Screen)**



  * **Why:** While not a "bookie," this is the premier odds screen used by professionals to visualize "steam" (sudden market movement). It aggregates data faster than consumer apps.

  * **Use Case:** Arbitrage and timing. It allows you to see the exact second a syndicate bets the line down at a sharp book so you can grab the "stale" line at a soft book before it moves.



-----



### **Category 2: The "Projections" (The Raw Fuel)**



*To calculate your own probabilities (e.g., "Patrick Mahomes over 285.5 yards"), you need data that goes deeper than box scores.*



**4. Pro Football Focus (PFF) Elite Data**



  * **Why:** They grade every single player on every single snap of every NFL/NCAA game.

  * **Use Case:** Your model shouldn't just know "RB gained 4 yards." It needs to know "RB gained 4 yards *despite* the O-Line missing a block." PFF data allows you to regress stats to the mean (e.g., predicting a QB will regress because his "Turnover Worthy Plays" were high, even if he didn't throw an interception).



**5. Baseball Savant (Statcast)**



  * **Why:** Owned by MLB, this provides the raw optical tracking data for every pitch (Exit Velocity, Launch Angle, Spin Rate).

  * **Use Case:** Finding "luck." If a batter is hitting .200 but his "Expected Batting Average" (xBA) based on exit velocity is .310, your model spots a value bet on his "Over Total Bases" prop before the market adjusts.



**6. KenPom (College Basketball)**



  * **Why:** The bible of college hoops efficiency. It adjusts for "tempo" (pace of play).

  * **Use Case:** A team might average 80 points per game, but KenPom reveals they play at a lightning pace. If they play a team that slows the game to a crawl, your model will accurately predict the "Under," whereas a basic stats model would bet the "Over."



**7. Evolving Hockey (NHL)**



  * **Why:** The gold standard for "Expected Goals" (xG) and "Wins Above Replacement" (WAR) in hockey.

  * **Use Case:** Hockey is high-variance. Evolving Hockey separates "goalie luck" from "team defense." It helps you bet on teams that are dominating possession but getting unlucky with bounces.



**8. Cleaning the Glass (NBA)**



  * **Why:** Filters out "garbage time" (end of game blowouts) which skews data on other sites.

  * **Use Case:** You need to know how a team performs *only* when their starters are on the floor. This source gives you the "Net Rating" of specific 5-man lineups, allowing you to smash a "2nd Quarter Spread" bet when you know a team's bench unit is weak.



-----



### **Category 3: The "News" (The Trigger)**



*Markets move instantly on injury news. You need to be faster than the books.*



**9. Underdog NBA (formerly FantasyLabs Twitter)**



  * **Why:** This feed is famously faster than the official waiver wire. They scrape beat writer tweets and update status instantly.

  * **Use Case:** The second a star player is ruled "Out," algorithms instantly bet the "Unders" on that team's total. You need this data feed plugged directly into your bot to beat the sportsbook's own adjustment.



-----



### **Category 4: The "Developer's Backbone"**



**10. SportsDataIO / Sportradar API**



  * **Why:** You need a rugged, enterprise-grade API to handle the boring stuff: schedules, weather delays, official grading, and roster changes.

  * **Use Case:** This is the skeleton of your database. It ensures your model doesn't bet on a game that has been rained out or cancelled.



### The "Sharp" Stack Summary



| Goal | Data Source |

| :--- | :--- |

| **Get True Odds** | **Pinnacle** (Global) & **Circa** (US) |

| **Catch Arb/Steam** | **SpankOdds** (The Screen) |

| **Model NFL** | **PFF** (Player Grades) |

| **Model NBA** | **Cleaning the Glass** (Garbage Time Removed) |

| **Model MLB** | **Baseball Savant** (Statcast) |

| **Fastest News** | **Underdog Network** (Twitter API) |



To understand how sharps use this "originating" data vs "soft" data to find an edge, this video breaks down the concept of "Closing Line Value" (CLV) using these exact sources.



[How to Find Sharp Betting Lines](https://www.google.com/search?q=https://www.youtube.com/watch%3Fv%3DhB9vtyXy1Rw)



This video is relevant because it visualizes how data from sources like **Pinnacle** is used to identify "fake" odds at soft books like DraftKings.



#######



If you are building an "Expert Sharp" engine and I cannot use the Top 10 "Gold Standards" (like Pinnacle, PFF, or KenPom), I would immediately turn to these next 10 sources.



These are not "second tier" sources; they are simply more specialized. Many professional syndicates rely on these just as heavily as the primary list to find edges in regression, weather, and officiating.



### **Category 1: The "Alternate" Market Makers**

*If Pinnacle and Circa are the Kings, these are the Barons. You need their odds to triangulate the true market price.*



**1. Betfair Exchange API (The Global Jury)**

* **Why:** While Pinnacle is a bookmaker, Betfair is an exchange (peer-to-peer).

* **The Data Point:** You use this for **"Weight of Money"**. If Pinnacle moves a line, you might not know if it’s one guy or the whole market. If Betfair moves, you can see the liquidity stack. It is the purest source of "Efficient Market Hypothesis" data in the world, specifically for Soccer and Tennis.



**2. Bookmaker.eu (The "Old School" Originator)**

* **Why:** Before DraftKings, there was Bookmaker (CRIS). They are famous for "never banning winners" and taking massive bets from professionals.

* **The Data Point:** **"The First Move."** Often, Bookmaker.eu will move a line on a key NFL number (like -3 to -3.5) *before* Pinnacle does. Your engine needs to watch this feed to predict when the rest of the world is about to change their odds.



### **Category 2: The "Regression" Engines**

*Standard stats tell you what happened. These sources tell you what "should" have happened.*



**3. ShotQuality (NBA & NCAA)**

* **Why:** They don't track made/missed shots; they track the *probability* of every shot going in based on x/y coordinates and defender distance.

* **The Data Point:** **"Luck Adjustment."** If a college team loses by 10, but ShotQuality says they won the "quality" battle by 8, your model identifies them as a massive value bet for the next game. This is the definition of "buying low."



**4. Dunks & Threes (NBA)**

* **Why:** The home of **EPM (Estimated Plus-Minus)**, which is widely considered the most accurate public all-in-one player metric, superior to PER or standard +/-.

* **The Data Point:** **"The Absence Impact."** When a star player sits, the market adjusts. But when a *role player* with a high EPM sits, the market often ignores it. Your engine uses EPM to catch value on spreads when an undervalued defensive stopper is injured.



**5. FTN Fantasy (Home of DVOA)**

* **Why:** "Football Outsiders" is gone; FTN now hosts the legendary **DVOA (Defense-adjusted Value Over Average)** metric.

* **The Data Point:** **"Play-by-Play Efficiency."** DVOA compares every single NFL play to a league baseline based on down and distance. It is the only way to objectively rank teams. (e.g., A 5-yard run on 3rd & 2 is worth way more than a 5-yard run on 3rd & 15).



**6. FanGraphs (MLB)**

* **Why:** The holy grail of baseball sabermetrics.

* **The Data Point:** **"Steamer & ZiPS Projections."** You do not write your own baseball projection code from scratch; you ingest these. They are the industry baseline for player performance. You also use their "Bullpen Usage" logs to fade teams whose best relievers are tired.



**7. FBref (Soccer)**

* **Why:** Powered by Opta data, this is the free standard for **xG (Expected Goals)** in soccer.

* **The Data Point:** **"Post-Shot xG."** This differentiates between "bad defense" and "bad goalkeeping." If a team is allowing 0.5 xG but conceding 2 goals per game, you bet on their defense to regress to the mean (improve), because the goalie variance will normalize.



### **Category 3: The "External" Variables**

*The game is played by humans, officiated by humans, and played outside. These variables ruin perfect math models if ignored.*



**8. Umpire Scorecards (MLB)**

* **Why:** It tracks every ball/strike call of every umpire and calculates their "Run Impact."

* **The Data Point:** **"The Umpire Over/Under Edge."** If a game has a total of 8.5 runs, but the home plate umpire is Pat Hoberg (who calls a perfect zone), the "true total" might be 8.0. If it's Angel Hernandez (erratic/hitter-friendly), it might be 9.0. This data alone can beat the closing line on Totals.



**9. RotoGrinders Weather (Kevin Roth)**

* **Why:** Generic weather apps are useless. You need to know "Wind density at stadium height." Kevin Roth is the industry meteorologist for betting.

* **The Data Point:** **"Wind Direction vs. Stadium Orientation."** A 15mph wind at Wrigley Field means "Over" if blowing out, and "Under" if blowing in. Your engine needs to ingest this specific vector data to adjust totals automatically.



**10. CollegeFootballData.com (CFB)**

* **Why:** The most robust free API for college football.

* **The Data Point:** **"EPA (Expected Points Added) on Early Downs."** In College Football, teams that stay "ahead of the chains" (high success rate on 1st/2nd down) are sustainable winners. Teams that rely on 3rd down "miracles" (explosive plays) are frauds. This API lets you filter out the lucky teams.



### The "B-Side" Sharp Stack

| Goal | Data Source |

| :--- | :--- |

| **Originating Odds** | **Bookmaker.eu** |

| **Market Liquidity** | **Betfair Exchange** |

| **NFL Efficiency** | **FTN (DVOA)** |

| **NBA True Talent** | **Dunks & Threes (EPM)** |

| **NCAA "Luck"** | **ShotQuality** |

| **MLB Projections** | **FanGraphs (ZiPS)** |

| **Soccer Model** | **FBref (xG)** |

| **Referees** | **Umpire Scorecards** |

| **Weather** | **RotoGrinders (Roth)** |

| **CFB Data** | **CollegeFootballData (EPA)** |



######



To build the "perfect" analytics engine, you cannot stop at the Top 20. The "Gold" and "Silver" tiers covered the basics (NFL/NBA/MLB/Soccer). To reach perfection, you must dominate the **Niche Markets** (where bookies have weaker models), the **Human Element** (Referees/Injuries), and **Atmospheric Physics**.



Here is the **Tier 3 (Niche Dominance)** and **Tier 4 (Granular Physics)** data stack. Adding these ensures your engine has no blind spots.



---



### **Category 5: The "Niche" Deep Dives**

*Bookmakers spend millions modeling the NFL. They spend $0 modeling 3rd tier Tennis or F1. This is where your engine prints money.*



**21. Tennis Abstract / Jeff Sackmann (Tennis)**

* **Why:** The absolute bible of tennis analytics.

* **The Data Point:** **"Surface Speed Adjustments + Elo."** Standard rankings (ATP/WTA) are flawed. Tennis Abstract’s "Elo ratings by surface" (Clay vs. Grass vs. Hard) are the only way to accurately price a match between a "Server" (good on grass) and a "Grinder" (good on clay).



**22. Data Golf (Golf)**

* **Why:** Standard "World Golf Rankings" are useless for betting. Data Golf uses "True Strokes Gained" adjusting for field strength and course difficulty.

* **The Data Point:** **"Course History vs. Current Form."** Some golfers are "Horse for Course" (play well at Augusta every year). Data Golf quantifies this stickiness. It also offers a **Live Model** that updates win probabilities after *every single shot*.



**23. UFCStats.com (MMA)**

* **Why:** The official statistical database of the UFC.

* **The Data Point:** **"Significant Strike Differential."** In MMA, "Control Time" is overrated by casuals. Damage wins fights. Your engine needs to track "Strikes Absorbed Per Minute." If a fighter absorbs 6.0+ strikes/min, they are a "fade" (bet against) regardless of their record.



**24. Oracle's Elixir (Esports - LoL)**

* **Why:** League of Legends is the biggest esports betting market.

* **The Data Point:** **"Early Game Rating (EGR)."** Some teams are great at the first 15 minutes (laning phase) but terrible at closing. Your engine uses EGR to bet the "First Tower" or "First Dragon" props, which are often mispriced by bookies who only look at match win %.



**25. FastF1 (Formula 1)**

* **Why:** A Python library that accesses the raw F1 Live Timing data.

* **The Data Point:** **"Corner Telemetry."** You can see if a driver is braking later than others in Practice sessions. If Max Verstappen is taking Turn 4 at 150mph and everyone else is at 142mph, you bet him for Pole Position before Qualifying starts.



---



### **Category 6: The "Zebra" Factor (Referees)**

*Referees have tendencies. Your engine must adjust the spread based on who is blowing the whistle.*



**26. NBAStuffer (NBA Referees)**

* **Why:** The most detailed database of NBA referee stats.

* **The Data Point:** **"Home/Away Bias."** Some refs (like Scott Foster) are historically notorious for favoring the road team or calling high-foul games. If a "Over" ref is paired with two fast-paced teams, you increase your total bet size.



**27. NFLPenalties.com (NFL Refs)**

* **Why:** Tracks every penalty called by every crew.

* **The Data Point:** **"Pass Interference Frequency."** If a crew calls Pass Interference at a high rate, you bet the "Over" (PI calls result in massive yardage gains). If they "let them play," you bet the "Under."



---



### **Category 7: The "Physio" Room (Advanced Injury)**

*Don't just know "if" they are playing. Know "how" they will play.*



**28. SIC Score (Sports Injury Central)**

* **Why:** Run by former NFL team doctors. They analyze video of injuries to grade health on a 1-100 scale.

* **The Data Point:** **"Effectiveness Rating."** A QB might be "Active," but if his SIC score is 60 (limited mobility), your engine knows to bet the "Under" on his Rushing Yards prop, even if the public expects him to be 100%.



---



### **Category 8: Atmospheric Physics (Weather)**

*Wind is more than just speed; it's density.*



**29. Meteomatics API**

* **Why:** Industrial-grade weather data used by energy companies.

* **The Data Point:** **"Air Density."** In the NFL and MLB, the ball travels further in less dense air (hot/humid). Standard apps just give temperature. Meteomatics gives you the exact air density index. Lower density = Bet the Over (Field Goals go further, Home Runs fly further).



---



### **Category 9: The "Sharp" Toolset**

*These are not "raw data" but "processed intelligence" essential for execution.*



**30. Unabated**

* **Why:** Founded by legends Captain Jack and Rufus Peabody.

* **The Tool:** **"The Massey-Peabody Power Ratings."** The industry gold standard for NFL team strength. You use this to sanity-check your own numbers. If your model differs from Massey-Peabody by 3+ points, your model is probably wrong.



**31. Props.cash**

* **Why:** The best visualizer for Player Props.

Python
import requests
import json
import time
import os
import logging
from google.cloud import storage
from fake_useragent import UserAgent

# LOGGING
logging.basicConfig(level=logging.INFO, format='%(asctime)s - [KAJI-BOVADA] - %(levelname)s - %(message)s')
logger = logging.getLogger("KajiBovada")

# CONFIG
PROJECT_ID = "veiled-vector-core"
BUCKET_NAME = f"veiled-vector-data-{PROJECT_ID}"
os.environ["GOOGLE_APPLICATION_CREDENTIALS"] = "credentials.json"
storage_client = storage.Client(project=PROJECT_ID)
bucket = storage_client.bucket(BUCKET_NAME)

# THE PUBLIC FEED (NFL)
URL = "https://www.bovada.lv/services/sports/event/v2/events/A/description/football/nfl"

ua = UserAgent()
HEADERS = {
    "User-Agent": ua.random,
    "Accept": "application/json"
}

def execute_heist():
    logger.info("Hitting Bovada Public Feed...")
    try:
        response = requests.get(URL, headers=HEADERS, timeout=15)
        
        if response.status_code == 200:
            data = response.json()
            
            # VALIDATION: Check for NFL events
            events = data[0].get('events', []) if data else []
            logger.info(f"Found {len(events)} events.")
            
            if len(events) > 0:
                # UPLOAD
                filename = f"bovada_nfl_{int(time.time())}.json"
                blob = bucket.blob(f"results/{filename}")
                blob.upload_from_string(json.dumps(data, indent=2), content_type='application/json')
                
                logger.info(f"LOOT SECURED: gs://{BUCKET_NAME}/results/{filename}")
                return True
            else:
                logger.warning("Feed returned 0 events. Season might be over or feed changed.")
                return False
        else:
            logger.error(f"Failed: {response.status_code}")
            return False

    except Exception as e:
        logger.error(f"Heist Failed: {e}")
        return False

if __name__ == "__main__":
    execute_heist()

Python
import json
from google.cloud import storage
import logging
import re

logging.basicConfig(level=logging.INFO)
logger = logging.getLogger("Normalizer")

PROJECT_ID = "veiled-vector-core"
BUCKET_NAME = f"veiled-vector-data-{PROJECT_ID}"
storage_client = storage.Client(project=PROJECT_ID)
bucket = storage_client.bucket(BUCKET_NAME)

# --- THE ROSETTA STONE ---
# Maps various bookmaker names to a Universal ID (NFL_Abbreviation)
TEAM_MAP = {
    "BUF Bills": "NFL_BUF", "Buffalo Bills": "NFL_BUF", "Bills": "NFL_BUF",
    "PIT Steelers": "NFL_PIT", "Pittsburgh Steelers": "NFL_PIT", "Steelers": "NFL_PIT",
    "KC Chiefs": "NFL_KC", "Kansas City Chiefs": "NFL_KC",
    # Add full league map here...
}

def normalize_draftkings(data):
    normalized = []
    events = data.get("events", [])
    for event in events:
        # DK Structure: "BUF Bills @ PIT Steelers"
        name = event.get("name", "")
        parts = name.split(" @ ")
        if len(parts) != 2: continue
        
        away_raw, home_raw = parts[0], parts[1]
        away_id = TEAM_MAP.get(away_raw, f"UNKNOWN_{away_raw}")
        home_id = TEAM_MAP.get(home_raw, f"UNKNOWN_{home_raw}")
        
        # Extract Odds (Simplified for Moneyline)
        # Note: DK structure is complex, this is a placeholder for the logic we verified
        # Real logic requires traversing 'markets' -> 'selections'
        
        normalized.append({
            "universal_id": f"{away_id}_at_{home_id}_{event['startEventDate'][:10]}",
            "book": "DraftKings",
            "home_team": home_id,
            "away_team": away_id,
            "raw_data": event # Keep raw for deep debugging
        })
    return normalized

def normalize_bovada(data):
    normalized = []
    # Bovada structure is nested: path -> events
    try:
        events = data[0]['events']
        for event in events:
            # Bovada description: "Buffalo Bills at Pittsburgh Steelers"
            desc = event.get('description', '')
            parts = desc.split(' at ')
            if len(parts) != 2: continue
            
            away_raw, home_raw = parts[0], parts[1]
            away_id = TEAM_MAP.get(away_raw, f"UNKNOWN_{away_raw}")
            home_id = TEAM_MAP.get(home_raw, f"UNKNOWN_{home_raw}")
            
            normalized.append({
                "universal_id": f"{away_id}_at_{home_id}", # Date logic needed
                "book": "Bovada",
                "home_team": home_id,
                "away_team": away_id,
                "raw_data": event
            })
    except:
        pass
    return normalized

def run_normalization():
    # 1. List most recent files
    blobs = list(bucket.list_blobs(prefix="results/"))
    
    dk_file = next((b for b in blobs if "draftkings" in b.name), None)
    bovada_file = next((b for b in blobs if "bovada" in b.name), None)
    
    master_ledger = []
    
    if dk_file:
        logger.info(f"Processing DraftKings: {dk_file.name}")
        data = json.loads(dk_file.download_as_text())
        master_ledger.extend(normalize_draftkings(data))
        
    if bovada_file:
        logger.info(f"Processing Bovada: {bovada_file.name}")
        data = json.loads(bovada_file.download_as_text())
        master_ledger.extend(normalize_bovada(data))
        
    # 2. Output the Golden Record
    if master_ledger:
        logger.info(f"Normalized {len(master_ledger)} events.")
        print(json.dumps(master_ledger[:3], indent=2)) # Show preview
        
        # Save to 'processed' folder
        blob = bucket.blob("processed/golden_record_latest.json")
        blob.upload_from_string(json.dumps(master_ledger), content_type='application/json')

if __name__ == "__main__":
    run_normalization()

Markdown
# STANDARD OPERATING PROCEDURE: DATA ACQUISITION (SOP-DA-001)

## 1. THE GOLDEN RULE: "Soft Targets First"
Never attempt to scrape a site (Selenium/Playwright) until you have exhausted API options.

**Priority Hierarchy:**
1.  **Public JSON Feeds (Tier 1):** Look for affiliate feeds (e.g., Bovada).
    * *Action:* Check `services/sports/event/v2/...` endpoints.
2.  **Mobile API Gateways (Tier 2):** Look for "Nash" or "CDN" endpoints used by mobile apps (e.g., DraftKings).
    * *Action:* Filter Network tab for `GET` requests returning JSON.
3.  **Internal/Hidden APIs (Tier 3):** Look for GraphQL or Auth-gated APIs.
    * *Action:* Requires header cloning (User-Agent, Referer, X-Client-Key).
4.  **The "Nuclear Option" (Tier 4):** Visual Scraping (Vision/Screenshots).
    * *Constraint:* Use ONLY if Tier 1-3 fail.

## 2. DATA NORMALIZATION STANDARD
All incoming data must be mapped to the **Universal Event ID**:
`SPORT_DATE_AWAY_HOME` (e.g., `NFL_2025-11-30_BUF_PIT`)

**Team Name Mapping:**
- "BUF" / "Bills" -> `NFL_BUF`
- "PIT" / "Steelers" -> `NFL_PIT`

## 3. PROVEN SOURCES (DO NOT RE-DISCOVER)
* **DraftKings:** Use `worker_dk.py` pattern (Nash API).
* **Bovada:** Use `worker_bovada.py` pattern (Public JSON).
* **CollegeFootballData:** Use Official API (Tier 1).

## 4. BANNED METHODS
* **Do NOT** use WebSockets without a specific subscription handshake.
* **Do NOT** parse HTML text for dynamic SPAs (React/Next.js); use Vision or API sniffing.
